![img-124.jpeg](img-124.jpeg)

## ZQ Calibration

The MPC command is used to initiate ZQ calibration, which calibrates the output driver impedance and CA/DQ ODT impedance across process, temperature, and voltage. ZQ calibration occurs in the background of device operation and is designed to eliminate any need for coordination between channels (that is, it allows for channel independence). ZQ calibration is required each time that the PU-Cal value (MR3-OP[0]) is changed. Additional ZQ CALIBRATION commands may be required as the voltage and temperature change in the system environment. CA ODT values (MR11-OP[6:4]) and DQ ODT values (MR11-OP[2:0]) may be changed without performing ZQ calibration, as long as the PU-Cal value doesn't change.
There are two ZQ calibration modes initiated with the MPC command: ZQCAL START and ZQCAL LATCH. ZQCAL START initiates the calibration procedure, and ZQCAL LATCH captures the result and loads it into the drivers.# Micron 

## 200b: x32 Automotive LPDDR4X/LPDDR4 SDRAM ZQ Calibration

A ZQCAL START command may be issued anytime the device is not in a power-down state. A ZQCAL LATCH command may be issued anytime outside of power-down after ${ }^{1} Z Q C A L$ has expired and all DQ bus operations have completed. The CA bus must maintain a deselect state during ${ }^{t} Z Q L A T$ to allow CA ODT calibration settings to be updated. The DQ calibration value will not be updated until ZQCAL LATCH is performed and ${ }^{t} Z Q L A T$ has been met. The following mode register fields that modify I/O parameters cannot be changed following a ZQCAL START command and before ${ }^{t} Z Q C A L$ has expired:

- PU-Cal (pull-up calibration $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}$ point)
- PDDS (pull-down drive strength and Rx termination)
- DQ ODT (DQ ODT value)
- CA ODT (CA ODT value)


## ZQCAL Reset

The ZQCAL RESET command resets the output impedance calibration to a default accuracy of $\pm 30 \%$ across process, voltage, and temperature. This command is used to ensure output impedance accuracy to $\pm 30 \%$ when ZQCAL START and ZQCAL LATCH commands are not used.

The ZQCAL RESET command is executed by writing MR10-OP[0] = 1B.

## Table 136: ZQ Calibration Parameters

| Parameter | Symbol | Min/Max | Value | Unit |
| :-- | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
| ZQCAL START to ZQCAL LATCH command interval | ${ }^{t} Z Q C A L$ | MIN | 1 | $\mu \mathrm{s}$ |
| ZQCAL LATCH to next valid command interval | ${ }^{t} Z Q L A T$ | MIN | MAX(30ns, 8nCK) | ns |
| ZQCAL RESET to next valid command interval | ${ }^{t} Z Q R E S E T$ | MIN | MAX(50ns, 3nCK) | ns |

Figure 120: ZQCAL Timing
![img-125.jpeg](img-125.jpeg)

Notes: 1. WRITE and PRECHARGE operations are shown for illustrative purposes. Any single or multiple valid commands may be executed within the ${ }^{t} Z Q C A L$ time and prior to latching the results.
2. Before the ZQCAL LATCH command can be executed, any prior commands that utilize the DQ bus must have completed. WRITE commands with DQ termination must be given enough time to turn off the DQ ODT before issuing the ZQCAL LATCH command. See the ODT section for ODT timing.

## Multichannel Considerations

The device includes a single ZQ pin and associated ZQ calibration circuitry. Calibration values from this circuit will be used by both channels according to the following protocol:

- The ZQCAL START command can be issued to either or both channels.- The ZQCAL START command can be issued when either or both channels are executing other commands, and other commands can be issued during ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{ZQCAL}$.
- The ZQCAL START command can be issued to both channels simultaneously.
- The ZQCAL START command will begin the calibration unless a previously requested ZQ calibration is in progress.
- If the ZQCAL START command is received while a ZQ calibration is in progress, the command will be ignored and the in-progress calibration will not be interrupted.
- The ZQCAL LATCH command is required for each channel.
- The ZQCAL LATCH command can be issued to both channels simultaneously.
- The ZQCAL LATCH command will latch results of the most recent ZQCAL START command provided ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{ZQCAL}$ has been met.
- ZQCAL LATCH commands that do not meet ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{ZQCAL}$ will latch the results of the most recently completed ZQ calibration.
- The ZQRESET MRW commands will only reset the calibration values for the channel issuing the command.

In compliance with complete channel independence, either channel may issue ZQCAL START and ZQCAL LATCH commands as needed without regard to the state of the other channel.

# ZQ External Resistor, Tolerance, and Capacitive Loading 

To use the ZQ CALIBRATION function, a 240 ohms, $\pm 1 \%$ tolerance external resistor must be connected between the ZQ pin and $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$.

If the system configuration shares the CA bus to form a x32 (or wider) channel, the ZQ pin of each die's x16 channel must use a separate ZQCAL resistor.

If the system configuration has more than one rank, and if the ZQ pins of both ranks are attached to a single resistor, then the SDRAM controller must ensure that the ZQCAL's don't overlap.

The total capacitive loading on the ZQ pin must be limited to 25pF. For example, if a system configuration shares a CA bus between $n$ channels to form an $n \times 16$ wide bus, and no means are available to control the ZQCAL separately for each channel (that is, separate CS, CKE, or CK), then each x16 channel must have a separate ZQCAL resistor. For a x32, two-rank system, each x16 channel must have its own ZQCAL resistor, but the ZQCAL resistor can be shared between ranks on each x16 channel. In this configuration, the CS signal can be used to ensure that the ZQCAL commands for Rank[0] and Rank[1] don't overlap.# 200b: x32 Automotive LPDDR4X/LPDDR4 SDRAM Frequency Set Points 

## Frequency Set Points

Frequency set points enable the CA bus to be switched between two differing operating frequencies with changes in voltage swings and termination values, without ever being in an untrained state, which could result in a loss of communication to the device. This is accomplished by duplicating all CA bus mode register parameters, as well as other mode register parameters commonly changed with operating frequency.
These duplicated registers form two sets that use the same mode register addresses, with read/write access controlled by MR bit FSP-WR (frequency set point write/read) and the operating point controlled by MR bit FSP-OP (FREQUENCY SET POINT operation). Changing the FSP-WR bit enables MR parameters to be changed for an alternate frequency set point without affecting the current operation.

Once all necessary parameters have been written to the alternate set point, changing the FSP-OP bit will switch operation to use all of the new parameters simultaneously (within ${ }^{1} \mathrm{FC}$ ), eliminating the possibility of a loss of communication that could be caused by a partial configuration change.
Parameters that have two physical registers controlled by FSP-WR and FSP-OP include those in the following table.

Table 137: Mode Register Function With Two Physical Registers

| MR Number | Operand | Function | Notes |
| :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
| MR1 | OP[2] | WR-PRE (Write preamble length) |  |
|  | OP[3] | RD-PRE (Read preamble type) |  |
|  | OP[6:4] | $n$ WR (Write-recovery for AUTO PRECHARGE command) |  |
|  | OP[7] | RD-PST (Read postamble length) |  |
| MR2 | OP[2:0] | RL (READ latency) |  |
|  | OP[5:3] | WL (WRITE latency) |  |
|  | OP[6] | WLS (WRITE latency set) |  |
| MR3 | OP[0] | PU-CAL (Pull-up calibration point) | 1 |
|  | OP[1] | WR-PST(Write postamble length) |  |
|  | OP[5:3] | PDDS (Pull-down drive strength) |  |
|  | OP[6] | DBI-RD (DBI-read enable) |  |
|  | OP[7] | DBI-WR (DBI-write enable) |  |
| MR11 | OP[2:0] | DQ ODT (DQ bus receiver on-die termination) |  |
|  | OP[6:4] | CA ODT (CA bus receiver on-die termination) |  |
| MR12 | OP[5:0] | $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}\left(\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}\right.$ setting) |  |
|  | OP[6] | $\mathrm{VR}_{\mathrm{CA}}\left(\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}\right.$ range) |  |

The FSP-WR and FSP-OP functions operate completely independently.

## On-Die Termination for the Command/Address Bus

The on-die termination (ODT) feature allows the device to turn on/off termination resistance for CK_t, $\mathrm{CK} \_\mathrm{c}, \mathrm{CS}$, and $\mathrm{CA}[5: 0]$ signals without the ODT control pin. The ODT feature is designed to improve signal integrity of the memory channel by allowing the DRAM controller to turn on and off termination resistance for any target DRAM devices via the mode register setting.
A simple functional representation of the DRAM ODT feature is shown below.

## Figure 125: ODT for CA

![img-130.jpeg](img-130.jpeg)

## ODT Mode Register and ODT State Table

ODT termination values are set and enabled via MR11. The CA bus (CK_t, CK_c, CS, CA[5:0]) ODT resistance values are set by MR11 OP[6:4]. The default state for the CA is ODT disabled.
ODT is applied on the CA bus to the CK_t, CK_c, CS, and CA signals. Generally only one termination load will be present even if multiple devices are sharing the command signals. In contrast to LPDDR4 where the ODT_CA input is used in combination with mode registers, LPDDR4X uses mode registers exclusively to enable CA termination. Before enabling CA termination via MR11, all ranks should have appropriate MR22 termination settings programmed. In a multi rank system, the terminating rank should be trained first, followed by the non-terminating $\operatorname{rank}(\mathrm{s})$.

Table 145: Command Bus ODT State

| CA ODT <br> MR11[6:4] | ODTD-CA <br> MR22 OP[5] | ODTE-CK <br> MR22 OP[3] | ODTE-CS <br> MR22 OP[4] | ODT State <br> for CA | ODT State <br> for CK | ODT State <br> for CS |
| :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
| Disabled $^{1}$ | Valid $^{2}$ | Valid $^{2}$ | Valid $^{2}$ | Off | Off | Off |
| Valid $^{2}$ | 0 | 0 | 0 | On | On | On |
| Valid $^{2}$ | 0 | 0 | 1 | On | On | Off |
| Valid $^{2}$ | 0 | 1 | 0 | On | Off | On |# Micron

# ODT for CA Update Time 

Figure 126: ODT for CA Setting Update Timing in 4-Clock Cycle Command
![img-131.jpeg](img-131.jpeg)# DQ On-Die Termination 

On-die termination (ODT) is a feature that allows the device to turn on/off termination resistance for each DQ, DQS, and DMI signal without the ODT control pin. The ODT feature is designed to improve signal integrity of the memory channel by allowing the DRAM controller to turn on and off termination resistance for any target DRAM devices during WRITE or MASK WRITE operation.
The ODT feature is off and cannot be supported in power-down and self refresh modes.
The switch is enabled by the internal ODT control logic, which uses the WRITE-1 or MASK WRITE-1 command and other mode register control information. The value of $R_{T T}$ is determined by the MR bits.

Figure 127: Functional Representation of DQ ODT
![img-132.jpeg](img-132.jpeg)

## ODT Mode Register

The ODT mode is enabled if MR11 OP[2:0] are non-zero. In this case, the value of $R_{T T}$ is determined by the settings of those bits. The ODT mode is disabled if MR11 OP[2:0] $=0$.

## Asynchronous ODT

When ODT mode is enabled in MR11 OP[2:0], DRAM ODT is always High-Z. The DRAM ODT feature is automatically turned ON asynchronously after a WRITE-1, MASK WRITE-1, or MPC[WRITE-FIFO] command. After the burst write is complete, the DRAM ODT turns OFF asynchronously. The DQ bus ODT control is automatic and will turn the ODT resistance on/off if DQ ODT is enabled in the mode register.

The following timing parameters apply when the DQ bus ODT is enabled:

- ODTLon, ${ }^{\text {ODTOn( }}$ (MIN), ${ }^{\text {ODTOn(MAX) }}$
- ODTLoff, ${ }^{\text {ODToff( }}$ (MIN), ${ }^{\text {ODToff(MAX) }}$

ODTL ${ }_{\text {ON }}$ is a synchronous parameter and is the latency from a CAS-2 command to the ${ }^{\text {ODTon }}$ reference. $\mathrm{ODTL}_{\mathrm{ON}}$ latency is a fixed latency value for each speed bin. Each speed bin has a different $\mathrm{ODTL}_{\mathrm{ON}}$ latency.

Minimum $\mathrm{R}_{\mathrm{TT}}$ turn-on time ( ${ }^{\mathrm{t}}$ ODTon(MIN)) is the point in time when the device termination circuit leaves High-Z and ODT resistance begins to turn on.

Maximum $\mathrm{R}_{\mathrm{TT}}$ turn on time ( ${ }^{\mathrm{t}}$ ODTon(MAX)) is the point in time when the ODT resistance is fully on.
${ }^{\mathrm{t}}$ ODTon(MIN) and ${ }^{\mathrm{t}}$ ODTon(MAX) are measured after $\mathrm{ODTL}_{\mathrm{ON}}$ latency is satisfied from CAS-2 command.

ODTL ${ }_{\text {OFF }}$ is a synchronous parameter and it is the latency from CAS-2 command to ${ }^{\text {t }}$ ODToff reference. $\mathrm{ODTL}_{\text {OFF }}$ latency is a fixed latency value for each speed bin. Each speed bin has a different $\mathrm{ODTL}_{\text {OFF }}$ latency.

Minimum $\mathrm{R}_{\mathrm{TT}}$ turn-off time ( ${ }^{\mathrm{t}}$ ODToff(MIN)) is the point in time when the device termination circuit starts to turn off the ODT resistance.

Maximum ODT turn off time ( ${ }^{\mathrm{t}}$ ODToff(MAX)) is the point in time when the on-die termination has reached High-Z.
${ }^{\mathrm{t}}$ ODToff(MIN) and ${ }^{\mathrm{t}}$ ODToff(MAX) are measured after $\mathrm{ODTL}_{\text {OFF }}$ latency is satisfied from CAS-2 command.# Micron 

Micron Confidential and Proprietary

DQ bus ODT will be disabled in power-down mode. In self refresh mode, the ODT will be turned off when CKE is LOW but will be enabled if CKE is HIGH and DQ ODT is enabled in the mode register.

## ODT During Write Leveling Mode

If ODT is enabled in MR11 OP[2:0] in write leveling mode, the device always provides the termination on DQS signals. DQ termination is always off in write leveling mode.

| Enabled | On | Off |

## Target Row Refresh Mode

The device limits the number of times that a given row can be accessed within a refresh period ( ${ }^{\text {REFW }}$ $\times 2$ ) prior to requiring adjacent rows to be refreshed. The maximum activate count (MAC) is the maximum number of activates that a single row can sustain within a refresh period before the adjacent rows need to be refreshed. The row receiving the excessive actives is the target row (TRn), the adjacent rows to be refreshed are the victim rows. When the MAC limit is reached on TRn, either the device receives all ( $\mathrm{R} \times 2$ ) REFRESH commands before another row activate is issued, or the device should be placed into targeted row refresh (TRR) mode. The TRR mode will refresh the rows adjacent to the TRn that encountered ${ }^{\text {t}}$ MAC limit.
If the device supports unlimited MAC value: MR24 OP[2:0] $=000$ and MR24 OP[3] $=1$, TARGET ROW REFRESH operation is not required. Even though the device allows to set MR24 OP[7] $=1$ : TRR mode enable, in this case the device behavior is vendor specific. For example, a certain device may ignore MRW command for entering/exiting TRR mode or a certain device may support commands related TRR mode. See vendor device data sheets for details about TRR mode definition at supporting unlimited MAC value case.

There could be a maximum of two target rows to a victim row in a bank. The cumulative value of the activates from the two target rows on a victim row in a bank should not exceed MAC value.
MR24 fields are required to support the new TRR settings. Setting MR24 OP[7] $=1$ enables TRR mode and setting MR24 OP[7] $=0$ disables TRR mode. MR24 OP[6:4] defines which bank (BAn) the target row is located in (refer to MR24 table for details).

The TRR mode must be disabled during initialization as well as any other device calibration modes. The TRR mode is entered from a DRAM idle state, once TRR mode has been entered, no other mode register commands are allowed until TRR mode is completed; however, setting MR24 OP[7] $=0$ to interrupt and reissue the TRR mode is allowed.
When enabled, TRR mode is self-clearing. The mode will be disabled automatically after the completion of defined TRR flow (after the third BAn precharge has completed plus ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{MRD}$ ). Optionally, the TRR mode can also be exited via another MRS command at the completion of TRR by setting MR24 OP[7] = 0 . If the TRR is exited via another MRS command, the value written to MR24 OP[6:4] are "Don't Care."# TRR Mode Operation 

1. The timing diagram depicts TRR mode. The following steps must be performed when TRR mode is enabled. This mode requires all three ACT (ACT1, ACT2, and ACT3) and three corresponding PRE commands (PRE1, PRE2, and PRE3) to complete TRR mode. PRECHARGE All (PREA) commands issued while the device is in TRR mode will also perform precharge to BAn and counts towards PREn command.
2. Prior to issuing the MRW command to enter TRR mode, the device should be in the idle state. MRW command must be issued with MR24 OP[7] $=1$ and MR24 OP[6:4] defining the bank in which the targeted row is located. All other MR24 bits should remain unchanged.
3. No activity is to occur with the device until ${ }^{1} \mathrm{MRD}$ has been satisfied. When ${ }^{1} \mathrm{MRD}$ has been satisfied, the only commands allowed BAn, until TRR mode has completed, are ACT and PRE.
4. The first ACT to the BAn with the TRn address can now be applied; no other command is allowed at this point. All other banks must remain inactive from when the first BAn ACT command is issued until $\left[\left(1.5 \times{ }^{1} \mathrm{RAS}\right)+{ }^{1} \mathrm{RP}\right]$ is satisfied.
5. After the first ACT to the BAn with the TRn address is issued, PRE to BAn is to be issued ( $1.5 \times{ }^{1} \mathrm{RAS}$ ) later; and then followed ${ }^{1} \mathrm{RP}$ later by the second ACT to the BAn with the TRn address.
6. After the second ACT to the BAn with the TRn address is issued, PRE to BAn is to be issued ${ }^{1} \mathrm{RAS}$ later and then followed ${ }^{1} \mathrm{RP}$ later by the third ACT to the BAn with the TRn address.
7. After the third ACT to the BAn with the TRn address is issued, PRE to BAn would be issued ${ }^{1} \mathrm{RAS}$ later. TRR mode is completed once ${ }^{1} \mathrm{RP}$ plus ${ }^{1} \mathrm{MRD}$ is satisfied.
8. TRR mode must be completed as specified to guarantee that adjacent rows are refreshed. Anytime the TRR mode is interrupted and not completed, the interrupted TRR mode must be cleared and then subsequently performed again. To clear an interrupted TRR mode, MR24 change is required with setting MR24 OP[7] = 0, MR24 OP[6:4] are "Don't Care," followed by three PRE to BAn, with ${ }^{1} \mathrm{RP}$ time in between each PRE command. The complete TRR sequence (steps 2-7) must be then reissued and completed to guarantee that the adjacent rows are refreshed.
9. A REFRESH command to the device, or entering self refresh mode, is not allowed while the device is in TRR mode.

Figure 129: Target Row Refresh Mode
![img-134.jpeg](img-134.jpeg)

Notes: 1. TRn is the targeted row.
2. Bank BAn represents the bank in which the targeted row is located.
3. TRR mode self-clears after ${ }^{1} \mathrm{MRD}+{ }^{1} \mathrm{RP}$ measured from the third BAn precharge PRE3 at clock edge Th4.
4. TRR mode or any other activity can be re-engaged after ${ }^{1} \mathrm{RP}+{ }^{1} \mathrm{MRD}$ from the third BAn precharge PRE3. PRE_ALL also counts if it is issued instead of PREn. TRR mode is cleared by the device after PRE3 to the BAn bank.# Micron 

5. ACTIVATE commands to BAn during TRR mode do not provide refresh support (the refresh counter is unaffected).
6. The device must restore the degraded row(s) caused by excessive activation of the targeted row (TRn) necessary to meet refresh requirements.
7. A new TRR mode must wait ${ }^{1} \mathrm{MRD}+{ }^{1} \mathrm{RP}$ time after the third precharge.
8. BAn may not be used with any other command.
9. ACT and PRE are the only allowed commands to BAn during TRR mode.
10. REFRESH commands are not allowed during TRR mode.
11. All timings are to be met by DRAM during TRR mode, such as ${ }^{1}$ FAW. Issuing ACT1, ACT2, and ACT3 counts towards ${ }^{1}$ FAW budget.

## Post-Package Repair

The device has fail row address repair as an optional post-package repair (PPR) feature and it is readable through MR25 OP[7:0].

PPR provides simple and easy repair method in the system and fail row address can be repaired by the electrical programming of Electrical-fuse scheme. The device can correct one row per bank with PPR.

Electrical-fuse cannot be switched back to un-fused states once it is programmed. The controller should prevent unintended PPR mode entry and repair.

## Failed Row Address Repair

The following is procedure of PPR:

1. Before entering PPR mode, all banks must be precharged.
2. Enable PPR using MR4 OP[4] $=1$ and wait ${ }^{1}$ MRD.
3. Issue ACT command with fail row address.
4. Wait ${ }^{\text {I}}$ PGM to allow the device repair target row address internally then issue PRECHARGE
5. Wait ${ }^{\text {I}}$ PGM_EXIT after PRECHARGE, which allows the device to recognize repaired row address RAn.
6. Exit PPR mode with setting MR4 OP[4] $=0$.
7. The device is ready for any valid command after ${ }^{\text {I}}$ PGMPST.
8. In more than one fail address repair case, repeat step 2 to 7 .

Once PPR mode is exited, to confirm whether the target row has correctly repaired, the host can verify the repair by writing data into the target row and reading it back after PPR exit with MR4 OP[4] $=0$ and ${ }^{\text {I}}$ PGMPST.

The following timing diagram shows PPR operation.Figure 130: Post-Package Repair Timing
![img-135.jpeg](img-135.jpeg)

Notes: 1. During ${ }^{1} \mathrm{PGM}$, any other commands (including refresh) are not allowed on each die.
2. With one PPR command, only one row can be repaired at one time per die.
3. When PPR procedure completes, reset procedure is required before normal operation.
4. During PPR, memory contents are not refreshed and may be lost.

Table 152: Post-Package Repair Timing Parameters

| Parameter | Symbol | Min | Max | Units |
| :-- | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
| PPR programming time | ${ }^{1} \mathrm{PGM}$ | 1000 | - | ms |
| PPR exit time | ${ }^{1} \mathrm{PGM} \_\mathrm{EXIT}$ | 15 | - | ns |
| New address setting time | ${ }^{1} \mathrm{PGMPST}$ | 50 | - | $\mu \mathrm{s}$ |# Read Preamble Training 

Read preamble training is supported through the MPC function.
This mode can be used to train or read level the DQS receivers. After read preamble training is enabled by MR13 OP[1] $=1$, the device will drive DQS_t LOW and DQS_c HIGH within ${ }^{1}$ SDO and remain at these levels until an MPC[READ DQ CALIBRATION] command is issued.
During read preamble training, the DQS preamble provided during normal operation will not be driven by the device. After the MPC[READ DQ CALIBRATION] command is issued, the device will drive DQS_t/DQS_c and DQ like a normal READ burst after RL and ${ }^{1}$ DQSCK. Prior to the MPC[READ DQ CALIBRATION] command, the device may or may not drive DQ[15:0] in this mode.
While in read preamble training mode, only READ DQ CALIBRATION commands may be issued.

- Issue an MPC[READ DQ CALIBRATION] command followed immediately by a CAS-2 command.
- Each time an MPC[READ DQ CALIBRATION] command followed by a CAS-2 is received by the device, a 16-bit data burst will, after the currently set RL, drive the eight bits programmed in MR32 followed by the eight bits programmed in MR40 on all I/O pins.
- The data pattern will be inverted for I/O pins with a 1 programmed in the corresponding invert mask mode register bit.
- Note that the pattern is driven on the DMI pins, but no DATA BUS INVERSION function is enabled, even if read DBI is enabled in the DRAM mode register.
- This command can be issued every ${ }^{1} \mathrm{CCD}$ seamlessly.
- The operands received with the CAS-2 command must be driven LOW.

Read preamble training is exited within ${ }^{1}$ SDO after setting MR13 OP[1] $=0$.

## Figure 131: Read Preamble Training

![img-136.jpeg](img-136.jpeg)

Note: 1. Read DQ calibration supports only BL16 operation.# Electrical Specifications 

## Absolute Maximum Ratings

Stresses greater than those listed in the table below may cause permanent damage to the device. This is a stress rating only, and functional operation of the device at these conditions, or any other conditions outside those indicated in the operational sections of this document, is not implied. Exposure to absolute maximum rating conditions for extended periods may adversely affect reliability.

Table 153: Absolute Maximum DC Ratings

| Parameter | Symbol | Min | Max | Unit | Notes |
| :-- | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
| $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 1}$ supply voltage relative to $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{SS}}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 1}$ | -0.4 | 2.1 | V | 1 |
| $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}$ supply voltage relative to $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{SS}}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}$ | -0.4 | 1.5 | V | 1 |
| $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$ supply voltage relative to $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{SS}}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$ | -0.4 | 1.5 | V | 1 |
| Voltage on any ball relative to $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{SS}}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{IN}}, \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OUT}}$ | -0.4 | 1.5 | V |  |
| Storage temperature | $\mathrm{T}_{\mathrm{STG}}$ | -55 | 125 | ${ }^{\circ} \mathrm{C}$ | 2 |

Notes: 1. For information about relationships between power supplies, see the Voltage Ramp and Device Initialization section.
2. Storage temperature is the case surface temperature on the center/top side of the device. For measurement conditions, refer to the JESD51-2 standard.

Operation or timing that is not specified is illegal. To ensure proper operation, the device must be initialized properly.

## Differential Input Voltage for CK

The minimum input voltage needs to satisfy both $\mathrm{V}_{\text {indiff_CK }}$ and $\mathrm{V}_{\text {indiff_CK }} / 2$ specification at input receiver and their measurement period is $1^{1} \mathrm{CK} . \mathrm{V}_{\text {indiff_CK }}$ is the peak-to-peak voltage centered on 0 volts differential and $\mathrm{V}_{\text {indiff_CK }} / 2$ is maximum and minimum peak voltage from 0 volts.Figure 134: CK Differential Input Voltage
![img-139.jpeg](img-139.jpeg)

Table 160: CK Differential Input Voltage

| Parameter | Symbol | 1600/1867 |  | 2133/2400/3200 |  | 3733/4267 |  | Unit | Note |
| :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
|  |  | Min | Max | Min | Max | Min | Max |  |  |
| CK differential input voltage | $\mathrm{V}_{\text {indiff_CK }}$ | 420 | - | 380 | - | 360 | - | mV | 1 |

Note: 1. The peak voltage of differential CK signals is calculated in a following equation.

- $\mathrm{V}_{\text {indiff_CK }}=$ (Maximum peak voltage) - (Minimum peak voltage)
- Maximum peak voltage $=\operatorname{MAX}(\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{t}))$
- Minimum peak voltage $=\operatorname{MIN}(\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{t}))$
- $\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{t})=\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{CK}_{-} \mathrm{t}}-\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{CK}_{-} \mathrm{c}}$


# Peak Voltage Calculation Method 

The peak voltage of differential clock signals are calculated in a following equation.

- $\mathrm{V}_{\text {IH.DIFF.peak }}$ voltage $=\operatorname{MAX}(\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{t}))$
- $\mathrm{V}_{\text {IL.DIFF.peak }}$ voltage $=\operatorname{MIN}(\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{t}))$
- $\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{t})=\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{CK}_{-} \mathrm{t}}-\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{CK}_{-} \mathrm{c}}$Figure 135: Definition of Differential Clock Peak Voltage
![img-140.jpeg](img-140.jpeg)

Note: 1. $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{REF}(\mathrm{CA})}$ is device internal setting value by $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{REF}}$ training.

## Differential Input Cross-Point Voltage

The cross-point voltage of differential input signals (CK_t, CK_c) must meet the requirements in table below. The differential input cross-point voltage $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{IX}}$ is measured from the actual cross-point of true and complement signals to the mid level.

Figure 138: $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{ix}}$ Definition (Clock)
![img-143.jpeg](img-143.jpeg)

Table 165: Cross-Point Voltage for Differential Input Signals (Clock)

| Parameter | Symbol | 1600/1867 |  | 2133/2400/3200 |  | 3733/4267 |  | Unit |
| :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
|  |  | Min | Max | Min | Max | Min | Max |  |
| Clock differential input cross-point voltage ratio | $\mathrm{V}_{\text {ix_CK_ratio }}$ | - | 25 | - | 25 | - | 25 | \% |

Notes: 1. $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{ix}, \mathrm{CK} \text { _ratio }}$ is defined by this equation: $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{ix}, \mathrm{CK} \text { _ratio }}=\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{ix}, \mathrm{CK} \text { _FR }} /\left|\operatorname{MIN}(\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{t}))\right|$
2. $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{ix}, \mathrm{CK} \text { _ratio }}$ is defined by this equation: $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{ix}, \mathrm{CK} \text { _ratio }}=\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{ix}, \mathrm{CK} \text { _RF }} / \mathrm{MAX}(\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{t}))$
3. $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{ix}, \mathrm{CK} \text { _FR }}$ is defined as delta between crosspoint (CK_t fall, CK_c rise) to $\operatorname{MIN}(\mathrm{f}(\mathrm{t})) / 2$.
4. In LPDDR4 un-terminated case, CK mid level is calculated as:

- High level $=\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$; Low level $=\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{SS}}$; Mid level $=\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ} / 2}$
- In LPDDR4 un-terminated case, mid level must be equal or lower than $369 \mathrm{mV}\left(33.6 \%\right.$ of $\left.\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}\right)$

5. Notes 1-4 apply to entire table.# 200b: x32 Automotive LPDDR4X/LPDDR4 SDRAM AC and DC Input Measurement Levels

## Output Slew Rate and Overshoot/Undershoot Specifications

## Single-Ended Output Slew Rate

Table 173: Single-Ended Output Slew Rate

| Parameter | Symbol | Value |  |  |
| :-- | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
|  |  | Min | Max | Units |
| Single-ended output slew rate $\left(\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}=\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}} \times 0.5\right)$ | SRQse | 3.0 | 9.0 | $\mathrm{V} / \mathrm{ns}$ |
| Output slew rate matching ratio (rise to fall) | - | 0.8 | 1.2 | - |

Notes: 1. $\mathrm{SR}=$ Slew rate; $\mathrm{Q}=$ Query output; se $=$ Single-ended signal.
2. Measured with output reference load.
3. The ratio of pull-up to pull-down slew rate is specified for the same temperature and voltage, over the entire temperature and voltage range. For a given output, it represents the maximum difference between pull-up and pull-down drivers due to process variation.
4. The output slew rate for falling and rising edges is defined and measured between $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OL}(\mathrm{AC})}=0.2 \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}(\mathrm{DC})}$ and $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}(\mathrm{AC})}=0.8 \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}(\mathrm{DC})}$.
5. Slew rates are measured under average SSO conditions with $50 \%$ of the DQ signals per data byte switching.
6. Notes $1-5$ apply to entire table.

Figure 144: Single-Ended Output Slew Rate Definition
![img-149.jpeg](img-149.jpeg)

## Differential Output Slew Rate

Table 174: Differential Output Slew Rate

| Parameter | Symbol | Value |  |  |
| :-- | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
|  |  | Min | Max | Units |
| Differential output slew rate $\left(\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}=\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}} \times 0.5\right)$ | SRQdiff | 6 | 18 | $\mathrm{V} / \mathrm{ns}$ |

Notes: 1. $\mathrm{SR}=$ Slew rate; $\mathrm{Q}=$ Query output; se $=$ Differential signal.
2. Measured with output reference load.
3. The output slew rate for falling and rising edges is defined and measured between $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OL}(\mathrm{AC})}=-0.8 \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}(\mathrm{DC})}$ and $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}(\mathrm{AC})}=0.8 \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}(\mathrm{DC})}$.
4. Slew rates are measured under average SSO conditions with $50 \%$ of the DQ signals per data byte switching.
5. Notes $1-4$ apply to entire table.Figure 145: Differential Output Slew Rate Definition

| :-- | :-- | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |

Notes: 1. $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD}}$ stands for $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}$ for $\mathrm{CA}[5: 0], \mathrm{CK} \_t, \mathrm{CS} \_\mathrm{n}, \mathrm{CKE}$, and ODT. $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD}}$ stands for $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$ for DQ, DMI, DQS_t, and DQS_c.
2. $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{SS}}$ stands for $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{SS}}$ for $\mathrm{CA}[5: 0], \mathrm{CK} \_t, \mathrm{CK} \_\mathrm{c}, \mathrm{CS} \_\mathrm{n}, \mathrm{CKE}$, and ODT. $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{SS}}$ stands for $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{SSQ}}$ for DQ, DMI, DQS_t, and DQS_c.
3. Maximum peak amplitude values are referenced from actual $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD}}$ and $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{SS}}$ values.
4. Maximum area values are referenced from maximum $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD}}$ and $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{SS}}$ values.

# Driver Output Timing Reference Load 

Timing reference loads are not intended as a precise representation of any particular system environment or depiction of an actual load presented by a production tester. System designers should use IBIS or other simulation tools to correlate the timing reference load to a system environment. Manufacturers correlate to their production test conditions, generally one or more coaxial transmission lines terminated at the tester electronics.

Figure 147: Driver Output Timing Reference Load
![img-152.jpeg](img-152.jpeg)

Note: 1. All output timing parameter values are reported with respect to this reference load; this reference load is also used to report slew rate.

## LVSTL I/O System

LVSTL I/O cells are comprised of a driver pull-up and pull-down and a terminator.Figure 148: LVSTL I/O Cell
![img-153.jpeg](img-153.jpeg)

To ensure that the target impedance is achieved, calibrate the LVSTL I/O cell as following example:

1. Calibrate the pull-down device against a 240 ohm resistor to $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$ via the ZQ pin.

- Set strength control to minimum setting
- Increase drive strength until comparator detects data bit is less than $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}} / 2$
- NMOS pull-down device is calibrated to 240 ohms

2. Calibrate the pull-up device against the calibrated pull-down device.

- Set $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}$ target and NMOS controller ODT replica via MRS ( $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}$ can be automatically controlled by ODT MRS)
- Set strength control to minimum setting
- Increase drive strength until comparator detects data bit is greater than $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}$ target
- NMOS pull-up device is calibrated to $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}$ target


# Figure 149: Pull-Up Calibration 

![img-154.jpeg](img-154.jpeg)# 200b: x32 Automotive LPDDR4X/LPDDR4 SDRAM Input/Output Capacitance

## Input/Output Capacitance

Table 177: Input/Output Capacitance

|  Parameter | Symbol | Min | Max | Unit | Notes  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
|  Input capacitance, CK_t and CK_c | $\mathrm{C}_{\mathrm{CK}}$ | 0.5 | 0.9 | pF |   |
|  Input capacitance delta, CK_t and CK_c | $\mathrm{C}_{\mathrm{DCK}}$ | 0 | 0.09 |  | 3  |
|  Input capacitance, all other input-only pins | $\mathrm{C}_{\mathrm{I}}$ | 0.5 | 0.9 |  | 4  |
|  Input capacitance delta, all other input-only pins | $\mathrm{C}_{\mathrm{DI}}$ | -0.1 | 0.1 |  | 5  |
|  Input/output capacitance, DQ, DMI, DQS_t, DQS_c | $\mathrm{C}_{\mathrm{IO}}$ | 0.7 | 1.3 |  | 6  |
|  Input/output capacitance delta, DQS_t, DQS_c | $\mathrm{C}_{\text {DDQS }}$ | 0 | 0.1 |  | 7  |
|  Input/output capacitance delta, DQ, DMI | $\mathrm{C}_{\text {DIO }}$ | -0.1 | 0.1 |  | 8  |
|  Input/output capacitance, ZQ pin | $\mathrm{C}_{\mathrm{ZQ}}$ | 0 | 5.0 |  |   |

Notes: 1. This parameter applies to LPDDR4 die only (does not include package capacitance). 2. This parameter is not subject to production testing; It is verified by design and characterization. The capacitance is measured according to JEP147 (procedure for measuring input capacitance using a vector network analyzer), with $\mathrm{V}*{\mathrm{DD1}}, \mathrm{V}*{\mathrm{DD2}}, \mathrm{V}*{\mathrm{DDQ}}$, and $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{SS}}$ applied; All other pins are left floating. 3. Absolute value of $\mathrm{C}*{\mathrm{CK} \_t}-\mathrm{C}*{\mathrm{CK} \_c}$. 4. $C*{I}$ applies to CS, CKE, and CA[5:0]. 5. $\mathrm{C}*{\mathrm{DI}}=\mathrm{C}*{\mathrm{I}}-0.5 \times\left(\mathrm{C}*{\mathrm{CK} \_t}+\mathrm{C}*{\mathrm{CK} \_c}\right)$; It does not apply to CKE. 6. DMI loading matches DQ and DQS. 7. Absolute value of $\mathrm{C}*{\mathrm{DQS} \_t}$ and $\mathrm{C}*{\mathrm{DQS} \_c}$. 8. $\mathrm{C}*{\mathrm{DIO}}=\mathrm{C}*{\mathrm{IO}}$ - Average ( $\mathrm{C}*{\mathrm{DQn}}, \mathrm{C}*{\mathrm{DMI}}, \mathrm{C}*{\mathrm{DQS} \_t}, \mathrm{C}*{\mathrm{DQS} \_c}$ ) in byte-lane. 9. Notes 1 and 2 apply to entire table.

## $\mathrm{I}_{\mathrm{DD}}$ Specifications

$I_{D D}$ values are for the entire operating voltage range, and all of them are for the entire standard temperature range.

Notes: 1. ODT disabled: MR11[2:0] = 000b.
2. $I_{D D}$ current specifications are tested after the device is properly initialized.
3. Measured currents are the summation of $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$ and $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}$.
4. Guaranteed by design with output load $=5 \mathrm{pF}$ and $R_{O N}=40 \mathrm{ohm}$.
5. The $1 x$ self refresh rate is the rate at which the device is refreshed internally during self refresh before going into the elevated temperature range.
6. This is the general definition that applies to full-array self refresh.
7. For all $I_{D D}$ measurements, $V_{I H C K E}=0.8 \times V_{D D 2} ; V_{I L C K E}=0.2 \times V_{D D 2}$.
8. LPDDR4: $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}, \mathrm{~V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}=1.06-1.17 \mathrm{~V} ; \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 1}=1.70-1.95 \mathrm{~V}$
9. LPDDR4X: $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}=1.06-1.17 \mathrm{~V} ; \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}=0.57-0.65 \mathrm{~V} ; \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 1}=1.70-1.95 \mathrm{~V}$# AC Timing

It also includes the AC noise impact for frequencies $>20 \mathrm{MHz}$ and a max voltage of 45 mV peak-to-peak from DC-20 MHz at a fixed temperature on the package. The voltage supply noise must comply with the component MIN/MAX DC operating conditions.
2. ${ }^{1}$ DQSCK_volt max delay variation as a function of DC voltage variation for $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$ and $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}$. The voltage supply noise must comply with the component MIN/MAX DC operating conditions. The voltage variation is defined as the MAX[ABS( ${ }^{1}$ DQSCK(MIN)@V1 - ${ }^{1}$ DQSCK(MAX)@V2), ABS( ${ }^{1}$ DQSCK(MAX)@V1 - ${ }^{1}$ DQSCK(MIN)@V2)]/ABS(V1 - V2).
3. ${ }^{1}$ DQSCK_temp MAX delay variation as a function of temperature.
4. The same voltage and temperature are applied to ${ }^{1}$ DQSCK_rank2rank.
5. ${ }^{1}$ DQSCK_rank2rank parameter is applied to multi-ranks per byte lane within a package consisting of the same design die.# Micron 

## 200b: x32 Automotive LPDDR4X/LPDDR4 SDRAM AC Timing

6. DQ-to-DQS differential jitter where the total includes the sum of deterministic and random timing terms for a specified BER.
7. The deterministic component of the total timing.
8. This parameter will be characterized and guaranteed by design.
9. ${ }^{1} \mathrm{QSL}$ describes the instantaneous differential output low pulse width on DQS_t - DQS_c, as measured from one falling edge to the next consecutive rising edge.
10. ${ }^{1} \mathrm{QSH}$ describes the instantaneous differential output high pulse width on DQS_t - DQS_c, as measured from one falling edge to the next consecutive rising edge.
11. This parameter is a function of input clock jitter. These values assume $\mathrm{MIN}^{1} \mathrm{CH}(\mathrm{ABS})$ and ${ }^{1} \mathrm{CL}(\mathrm{ABS})$. When the input clock jitter $\mathrm{MIN}^{1} \mathrm{CH}(\mathrm{ABS})$ and ${ }^{1} \mathrm{CL}(\mathrm{ABS})$ is 0.44 or greater than ${ }^{1} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{AVG})$, the minimum value of ${ }^{1} \mathrm{QSL}$ will be ${ }^{1} \mathrm{CL}(\mathrm{ABS})$ - 0.04 and ${ }^{1} \mathrm{QSH}$ will be ${ }^{1} \mathrm{CH}(\mathrm{ABS})-0.04$.

## CA Rx Voltage and Timing

The command and address (CA), including CS input receiver compliance mask for voltage and timing, is shown in the CA Receiver (Rx) Mask figure below. All CA and CS signals apply the same compliance mask and operate in single data rate mode.

The CA input Rx mask for voltage and timing is applied across all pins, as shown in the figure below. The Rx mask defines the area that the input signal must not encroach if the DRAM input receiver is expected to successfully capture a valid input signal; it is not the valid data eye.

Figure 152: CA Receiver (Rx) Mask
![img-157.jpeg](img-157.jpeg)Figure 153: Across Pin $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF (CA) }}$ Voltage Variation
![img-158.jpeg](img-158.jpeg)
$\mathrm{V}_{\text {CENT_CA(pin mid) }}$ is defined as the midpoint between the largest $\mathrm{V}_{\text {CENT_CA }}$ voltage level and the smallest $\mathrm{V}_{\text {CENT_CA }}$ voltage level across all CA and CS pins for a given DRAM component. Each CAV CENT level is defined by the center, which is, the widest opening of the cumulative data input eye, as depicted in the figure above. This clarifies that any DRAM component level variation must be accounted for within the CA Rx mask. The component-level $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF }}$ will be set by the system to account for $\mathrm{R}_{\mathrm{CIN}}$ and ODT settings.

# Clock Specification 

The specified clock jitter is a random jitter with Gaussian distribution. Input clocks violating minimum or maximum values may result in device malfunction.

Table 206: Definitions and Calculations

| Symbol | Description | Calculation | Notes |
| :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
| ${ }^{t} \mathrm{CK}($ avg) and $n \mathrm{CK}$ | The average clock period across any consecutive 200-cycle window. Each clock period is calculated from rising clock edge to rising clock edge. <br> Unit ${ }^{t} \mathrm{CK}($ avg) represents the actual clock average ${ }^{t} \mathrm{CK}($ avg) of the input clock under operation. Unit $n \mathrm{CK}$ represents one clock cycle of the input clock, counting from actual clock edge to actual clock edge. <br> ${ }^{t} \mathrm{CK}($ avg) can change no more than $\pm 1 \%$ within a 100 -clock-cycle window, provided that all jitter and timing specifications are met. | ${ }^{t} \mathrm{CK}(\text { avg })=\sum_{\mathrm{j}=1}^{\mathrm{N}}{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CK}_{\mathrm{j}} / \mathrm{N}$ <br> Where $\mathrm{N}=200$ |  |
| ${ }^{t} \mathrm{CK}($ abs $)$ | The absolute clock period, as measured from one rising clock edge to the next consecutive rising clock edge. |  | 1 |
| ${ }^{t} \mathrm{CH}($ avg $)$ | The average HIGH pulse width, as calculated across any 200 consecutive HIGH pulses. | ${ }^{t} \mathrm{CH}(\mathrm{avg})=\left(\sum_{\mathrm{j}=1}^{\mathrm{N}}{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CH}_{\mathrm{j}}\right) /\left(\mathrm{N} \times{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})\right)$ <br> Where $\mathrm{N}=200$ |  |
| ${ }^{t} \mathrm{CL}(\mathrm{avg})$ | The average LOW pulse width, as calculated across any 200 consecutive LOW pulses. | ${ }^{t} \mathrm{CL}(\mathrm{avg})=\left(\sum_{\mathrm{j}=1}^{\mathrm{N}}{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CL}_{\mathrm{j}}\right) /\left(\mathrm{N} \times{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})\right)$ <br> Where $\mathrm{N}=200$ |  |
| ${ }^{t}$ JIT(per) | The single-period jitter defined as the largest deviation of any signal ${ }^{t} \mathrm{CK}$ from ${ }^{t} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})$. | ${ }^{t} \mathrm{JIT}(\mathrm{per})=\min / \max$ of $\left.{ }^{t} \mathrm{CK}_{\mathrm{i}}-{ }^{t} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})\right)$ <br> Where $\mathrm{i}=1$ to 200 | 1 |
| ${ }^{t}$ JIT(per),act | The actual clock jitter for a given system. |  |  |
| ${ }^{1}$ JIT(per), allowed | The specified clock period jitter allowance. |  |  |
| ${ }^{t}$ JIT(cc) | The absolute difference in clock periods between two consecutive clock cycles. ${ }^{t}$ JIT(cc) defines the cycle-to-cycle jitter. | ${ }^{t} \mathrm{JIT}(\mathrm{cc})=\max$ of $\left.{ }^{t} \mathrm{CK}_{\mathrm{i}+1}-{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CK}_{\mathrm{i}}\right)$ | 1 |
| ${ }^{t}$ ERR(nper) | The cumulative error across $n$ multiple consecutive cycles from ${ }^{t} \mathrm{CK}($ avg). | ${ }^{t} \mathrm{ERR}(\mathrm{nper})=\left(\sum_{\mathrm{j}=1}^{\mathrm{i}+\mathrm{n}-1}{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CK}_{\mathrm{j}}\right)-\left(\mathrm{n} \times{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})\right)$ | 1 |# Micron 

200b: x32 Automotive LPDDR4X/LPDDR4 SDRAM Clock Period Jitter

Table 206: Definitions and Calculations (Continued)

| Symbol | Description | Calculation | Notes |
| :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
| ${ }^{1}$ ERR(nper),act | The actual clock jitter over $n$ cycles for a given system. |  |  |
| ${ }^{1}$ ERR(nper), allowed | The specified clock jitter allowance over $n$ cycles. |  |  |
| ${ }^{1}$ ERR(nper), min | The minimum ${ }^{1}$ ERR(nper). | ${ }^{1}$ ERR $($ nper $), \min =(1+0.68 \mathrm{LN}(\mathrm{n})) \times{ }^{1} \mathrm{JIT}$ (per),min | 2 |
| ${ }^{1}$ ERR(nper), max | The maximum ${ }^{1}$ ERR(nper). | ${ }^{1}$ ERR $($ nper $), \max =(1+0.68 \mathrm{LN}(\mathrm{n})) \times{ }^{1} \mathrm{JIT}$ (per),max | 2 |
| ${ }^{1} \mathrm{JIT}($ duty $)$ | Defined with absolute and average specifications for ${ }^{1} \mathrm{CH}$ and ${ }^{1} \mathrm{CL}$, respectively. | ${ }^{1} \mathrm{JIT}($ duty $), \min =$ <br> $\operatorname{MIN}\left(\left({ }^{1} \mathrm{CH}(\mathrm{abs}), \min -{ }^{1} \mathrm{CH}(\mathrm{avg}), \min \right)\right.$, <br> $\left({ }^{1} \mathrm{CL}(\mathrm{abs}), \min -{ }^{1} \mathrm{CL}(\mathrm{avg}), \min \right) \times{ }^{1} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})$ <br> ${ }^{1} \mathrm{JIT}($ duty $), \max =$ <br> $\operatorname{MAX}\left({ }^{1} \mathrm{CH}(\mathrm{abs}), \max -{ }^{1} \mathrm{CH}(\mathrm{avg}), \max \right.$, <br> $\left({ }^{1} \mathrm{CL}(\mathrm{abs}), \max -{ }^{1} \mathrm{CL}(\mathrm{avg}), \max \right) \times{ }^{1} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})$ |  |

Notes: 1. Not subject to production testing.
2. Using these equations, ${ }^{1}$ ERR(nper) tables can be generated for each ${ }^{1} \mathrm{JIT}$ (per),act value.

## ${ }^{1} \mathbf{C K}($ abs), ${ }^{1} \mathbf{C H}($ abs), and ${ }^{1} \mathbf{C L}($ abs)

These parameters are specified with their average values; however, the relationship between the average timing and the absolute instantaneous timing (defined in the following table) is applicable at all times.

Table 207: ${ }^{1} \mathbf{C K}($ abs), ${ }^{1} \mathbf{C H}($ abs), and ${ }^{1} \mathbf{C L}($ abs) Definitions

| Parameter | Symbol | Minimum | Unit |
| :-- | :--: | :-- | :--: |
| Absolute clock period | ${ }^{1} \mathrm{CK}($ abs $)$ | ${ }^{1} \mathrm{CK}($ avg $), \min +{ }^{1} \mathrm{JIT}($ per $), \min$ | $\mathrm{ps}^{1}$ |
| Absolute clock HIGH pulse width | ${ }^{1} \mathrm{CH}($ abs $)$ | ${ }^{1} \mathrm{CH}($ avg $), \min +{ }^{1} \mathrm{JIT}($ duty $), \min ^{2} /{ }^{1} \mathrm{CK}($ avg $), \min$ | ${ }^{1} \mathrm{CK}($ avg $)$ |
| Absolute clock LOW pulse width | ${ }^{1} \mathrm{CL}($ abs $)$ | ${ }^{1} \mathrm{CL}($ avg $), \min +{ }^{1} \mathrm{JIT}($ duty $), \min ^{2} /{ }^{1} \mathrm{CK}($ avg $), \min$ | ${ }^{1} \mathrm{CK}($ avg $)$ |

Notes: 1. ${ }^{1} \mathrm{CK}($ avg $)$,min is expressed in ps for this table.
2. ${ }^{1} \mathrm{JIT}($ duty $), \min$ is a negative value.

## Clock Period Jitter

LPDDR4 devices can tolerate some clock period jitter without core timing parameter derating. This section describes device timing requirements with clock period jitter ( ${ }^{1} \mathrm{JIT}$ (per)) in excess of the values found in the AC Timing table. Calculating cycle time derating and clock cycle derating are also described.

## Clock Period Jitter Effects on Core Timing Parameters

Core timing parameters ( ${ }^{1} \mathrm{RCD},{ }^{1} \mathrm{RP},{ }^{1} \mathrm{RTP},{ }^{1} \mathrm{WR},{ }^{1} \mathrm{WRA},{ }^{1} \mathrm{WTR},{ }^{1} \mathrm{RC},{ }^{1} \mathrm{RAS},{ }^{1} \mathrm{RRD},{ }^{1} \mathrm{FAW}$ ) extend across multiple clock cycles. Clock period jitter impacts these parameters when measured in numbers of clock cycles. Within the specification limits, the device is characterized and verified to support ${ }^{1} n \mathrm{PARAM}=\mathrm{RU}\left[{ }^{1} \mathrm{PARAM} /{ }^{1} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})\right]$. During device operation where clock jitter is outside specification# Micron 

200b: x32 Automotive LPDDR4X/LPDDR4 SDRAM Clock Period Jitter
limits, the number of clocks, or ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})$, may need to be increased based on the values for each core timing parameter.

## Cycle Time Derating for Core Timing Parameters

For a given number of clocks ( ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} n$ PARAM), when ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})$ and ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{ERR}\left({ }^{\mathrm{t}} n\right.$ PARAM), act exceed ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{ERR}\left({ }^{\mathrm{t}} n\right.$ PARAM), allowed, cycle time derating may be required for core timing parameters.
CycleTimeDerating $=\max \left\{\frac{\left[^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{PARAM}+{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{ERR}\left({ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{n}\right.\right. \text { PARAM),act }}{{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{nPARAM}}-\mathrm{tCK}(\mathrm{avg})\right\} 0\}$
Cycle time derating analysis should be conducted for each core timing parameter. The amount of cycle time derating required is the maximum of the cycle time deratings determined for each individual core timing parameter.

## Clock Cycle Derating for Core Timing Parameters

For each core timing parameter and a given number of clocks ( ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} n$ PARAM), clock cycle derating should be specified with ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{JIT}$ (per).

For a given number of clocks ( ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} n$ PARAM), when ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})$ plus ( ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{ERR}\left({ }^{\mathrm{t}} n\right.$ PARAM),act) exceed the supported cumulative ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{ERR}\left({ }^{\mathrm{t}} n\right.$ PARAM), allowed, derating is required. If the equation below results in a positive value for a core timing parameter ( ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CORE}$ ), the required clock cycle derating will be that positive value (in clocks).

$$
\text { ClockCycleDerating }=\operatorname{RU}\left\{\frac{{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \text { PARAM }+{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \text { ERR }\left({ }^{\mathrm{t}} \text { nPARAM),act }-{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \text { ERR }\left({ }^{\mathrm{t}} \text { nPARAM),allowed } \mathrm{t}_{\mathrm{CK}}(\mathrm{avg})\right.}{}-\mathrm{t}_{\mathrm{nPARAM}}\right.
$$

Cycle-time derating analysis should be conducted for each core timing parameter.

## Clock Jitter Effects on Command/Address Timing Parameters

Command/address timing parameters ( ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{IS},{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{IH},{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{ISb},{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{IHb}$ ) are measured from a command/address signal (CS or CA[5:0]) transition edge to its respective clock signal (CK_t/CK_c) crossing. The specification values are not affected by the ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{JIT}$ (per) applied, because the setup and hold times are relative to the clock signal crossing that latches the command/address. Regardless of clock jitter values, these values must be met.

## Clock Jitter Effects on READ Timing Parameters

## ${ }^{\text {t }}$ RPRE

When the device is operated with input clock jitter, ${ }^{\text {t }}$ RPRE must be derated by the ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{JIT}$ (per),act,max of the input clock that exceeds ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{JIT}$ (per),allowed,max. Output deratings are relative to the input clock:
${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{RPRE}($ min, derated $)=0.9-\left\{\frac{{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{JIT}(\mathrm{per}) \text {,act,max }}{{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})}\right\}$
For example, if the measured jitter into a LPDDR4 device has ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})=625 \mathrm{ps},{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{JIT}$ (per),act,min =-xx, and ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{JIT}$ (per),act, max $=+\mathrm{xx}$ ps, then ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{RPRE}$,min,derated $=0.9-\left({ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{JIT}(\mathrm{per})\right.$,act,max -
${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{JIT}$ (per),allowed,max) $/{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})=0.9-(\mathrm{xx}-\mathrm{xx}) / \mathrm{xx}=\mathrm{yy}{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})$.
${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{LZ}(\mathrm{DQ}),{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{HZ}(\mathrm{DQ}),{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{DQSCK},{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{LZ}(\mathrm{DQS}),{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{HZ}(\mathrm{DQS})$# Micron 

200b: x32 Automotive LPDDR4X/LPDDR4 SDRAM

These parameters are measured from a specific clock edge to a data signal transition ( $\mathrm{DM} n$ or $\mathrm{DQ} m$, where: $n=0,1$; and $m=0-15$, and specified timings must be met with respect to that clock edge. Therefore, they are not affected by ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{JIT}$ (per).

## ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{QSH},{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{QSL}$

These parameters are affected by duty cycle jitter, represented by ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CH}$ (abs)min and ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CL}$ (abs)min. These parameters determine the absolute data-valid window at the device pin. The absolute minimum data-valid window at the device pin $=\operatorname{MIN}\left\{\left({ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{QSH}(\right.\right.$ (abs)min - ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{DQSQmax}$ ), $\left({ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{QSL}(\right.$ abs)min ${ }^{\mathrm{t}}$ DQSQmax) $\}$. This minimum data valid window must be met at the target frequency regardless of clock jitter.

## ${ }^{\text {t }}$ RPST

${ }^{\mathrm{t}}$ RPST is affected by duty cycle jitter, represented by ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CL}$ (abs). Therefore, ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{RPST}$ (abs)min can be specified by ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CL}(\mathrm{abs}) \mathrm{min} .{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{RPST}(\mathrm{abs}) \mathrm{min}={ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CL}(\mathrm{abs}) \mathrm{min}-0.05={ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{QSL}(\mathrm{abs}) \mathrm{min}$.

## Clock Jitter Effects on WRITE Timing Parameters

## ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{DS},{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{DH}$

These parameters are measured from a data signal (DMIn orDQm, where $n=0,1$ and $m=0-15$ ) transition edge to its respective data strobe signal (DQSn_t, DQSn_c: $n=0,1$ ) crossing. The specification values are not affected by the amount of ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{JIT}$ (per) applied, because the setup and hold times are relative to the data strobe signal crossing that latches the command/address. Regardless of clock jitter values, these values must be met.

## ${ }^{\mathrm{t}}$ DSS, ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{DSH}$

These parameters are measured from a data signal (DQS_t, DQSn_c) crossing to its respective clock signal (CK_t, CK_c) crossing. When the device is operated with input clock jitter, this parameter needs to be derated by the actual $\mathrm{t}_{\mathrm{JIT}(\text { per }) \text { act }}$ of the input clock in excess of the allowed period jitter $\mathrm{t}_{\mathrm{JIT} \text { (per)allowed. }}$

## ${ }^{\mathrm{t}}$ DQSS

${ }^{\mathrm{t}}$ DQSS is measured from a data strobe signal (DQSn_t, DQSn_c) crossing to its respective clock signal (CK_t, CK_c) crossing. When the device is operated with input clock jitter, this parameter must be derated by the actual ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{JIT}$ (per),act of the input clock in excess of ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{JIT}$ (per)allowed.
${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{DQSS}(\min$, derated $)=0.75-\left(\frac{\mathrm{t}_{\mathrm{JIT}(\text { per }) \text {,act,min }}-\mathrm{t}_{\mathrm{JIT}(\text { per }) \text {,allowed, } \min }}{{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})}\right.$
${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{DQSS}(\max$, derated $)=1.25-\left(\frac{\mathrm{t}_{\mathrm{JIT}(\text { per }) \text {,act,max }}}{}\right.$- ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{JIT}$ (per), allowed, max ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})$
For example, if the measured jitter into an LPDDR4 device has ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})=625 \mathrm{ps},{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{JIT}$ (per),act,min = -xxps, and ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{JIT}$ (per),act, $\max =+\mathrm{xx}$ ps, then:
${ }^{\mathrm{t}}$ DQSS, $($ min, derated $)=0.75-(-x x+y y) / 625=x x x x{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})$
${ }^{\mathrm{t}}$ DQSS, $($ max, derated $)=1.25-(\mathrm{xx}-\mathrm{yy}) / 625=x x x x{ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{CK}(\mathrm{avg})$# LPDDR4 $1.10 \mathrm{~V} \mathrm{~V}_{\text {DDQ }}$ 

This section defines LPDDR4 specifications to enable $1.10 \mathrm{~V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$ operation of LPDDR4 devices.

## Mode Register Definition - LPDDR4

Mode register definitions are provided in the Mode Register Assignments table. In the access column of the table, R indicates read-only; W indicates write-only; R/W indicates read- or write-capable or enabled. The MRR command is used to read from a register. The MRW command is used to write to a register.

Notes: 1. RZQI MR value, if supported, will be valid after the following sequence:

- Completion of MPC[ZQCAL START] command to either channel
- Completion of MPC[ZQCAL LATCH] command to either channel then ${ }^{1}$ ZQLAT is satisfied

RZQI value will be lost after reset.
2. If $Z Q$ is connected to $V_{S S Q}$ to set default calibration, OP[4:3] must be set to 01b. If $Z Q$ is not connected to $V_{S S Q}$, either $O P[4: 3]=01 b$ or $O P[4: 3]=10 b$ might indicate a $Z Q$ pin assembly error. It is recommended that the assembly error be corrected.
3. In the case of possible assembly error, the device will default to factory trim settings for $R_{O N}$, and will ignore ZQ CALIBRATION commands. In either case, the device may not function as intended.
4. If the ZQ pin self-test returns OP[4:3] = 11b, the device has detected a resistor connected to the ZQ pin. However, this result cannot be used to validate the ZQ resistor value or that the ZQ resistor meets the specified limits (that is, $240 \Omega \pm 1 \%$ ).
5. See byte mode addendum spec for byte mode latency details.# Micron

6. Byte mode latency for 2 Ch . x 16 device is only allowed when it is stacked in a same package with byte mode device.
7. CATR indicates whether CA for the rank will be terminated or not as a result of ODTCA pad connection and MR22 OP[5] settings for x16 devices, MR22 OP[7:5] settings for byte mode devices.

2. There are two physical registers assigned to each bit of this MR parameter, designated set point 0 and set point 1. Only the registers for the set point determined by the state of the FSP-WR bit (MR13 OP[6]) will be written to with an MRW command to this MR address, or read from with an MRR command to this address.
3. There are two physical registers assigned to each bit of this MR parameter, designated set point 0 and set point 1.The device will operate only according to the values stored in the registers for the active set point, for example, the set point determined by the state of the FSP-OP bit (MR13 OP[7]). The values in the registers for the inactive set point will be determined by the state of the FSP-OP bit (MR13 OP[7]). The values in the registers for the inactive set point will be ignored by the device, and may be changed without affecting device operation.
4. For dual channel device, PU-CAL (MR3-OP[0]) must be set the same for both channels on a die. The SDRAM will read the value of only one register (Ch.A or Ch.B), vendor-specific, so both channels must be set the same.
5. $1.5 \times{ }^{1} \mathrm{CK}$ apply $>1.6 \mathrm{GHz}$ clock.# Micron

6. If MR3 OP[2] is set to 1 b , PPR protection mode is enabled. The PPR protection bit is a sticky bit and can only be set to 0 b by a power on reset. MR4 OP[4] controls entry to PPR mode. If PPR protection is enabled then the DRAM will not allow writing of 1 b to MR4 OP[4].

The range (range[0] or range[1]) must be selected when setting the $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{REF}(\mathrm{CA})}$ register. The value, once set, will be retained until overwritten or until the next power-on or reset event.

The values in the registers for the inactive set point will be ignored by the device, and may be changed without affecting device operation.

2. The range may be selected in each of the MR14 or MR12 registers by setting OP[6] appropriately.
3. Each of the MR14 or MR12 registers represents either FSP[0] or FSP[1]. Two frequency set points each for CA and DQ are provided to allow for faster switching between terminated and unterminated operation or between different high-frequency settings, which may use different terminations values.
4. Notes 1-3 apply to entire table.# Micron

200b: x32 Automotive LPDDR4X/LPDDR4 SDRAM Mode Register Definition - LPDDR4

| :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
| ODTD for x8_2ch |  | ODTD-CA | ODTE-CS | ODTE-CK | SOC ODT |  |  |

Table 220: MR22 Register Information

| Function | Type | OP | Data | Notes |
| :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
| SOC ODT (controller ODT value for $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}$ calibration) | Write-only | OP[2:0] | 000b: Disable (default) | $1,2,3$ |
|  |  |  | 001b: $\mathrm{R}_{\mathrm{ZO}} / 1$ |  |
|  |  |  | 010b: $\mathrm{R}_{\mathrm{ZO}} / 2$ |  |
|  |  |  | 011b: $\mathrm{R}_{\mathrm{ZO}} / 3$ |  |
|  |  |  | 100b: $\mathrm{R}_{\mathrm{ZO}} / 4$ |  |
|  |  |  | 101b: $\mathrm{R}_{\mathrm{ZO}} / 5$ |  |
|  |  |  | 110b: $\mathrm{R}_{\mathrm{ZO}} / 6$ |  |
|  |  |  | 111b: RFU |  |
| ODTE-CK (CK ODT enabled for non-terminating rank) | Write-only | OP[3] | 0b: ODT-CK override disabled (default) | $2,3,4,6,8$ |
|  |  |  | 1b: ODT-CK override enabled |  |
| ODTE-CS (CS ODT enabled for non-terminating rank) | Write-only | OP[4] | 0b: ODT-CS override disabled (default) | $2,3,5,6,8$ |
|  |  |  | 1b: ODT-CS override enabled |  |
| ODTD-CA (CA ODT termination disable) | Write-only | OP[5] | 0b: CA ODT obeys ODT_CA bond pad (default) | $2,3,6,7,8$ |
|  |  |  | 1b: CA ODT disabled |  |
| ODTD for x8_2ch (Byte) mode | Write-only | OP[7:6] | See Byte Mode section |  |

Notes: 1. All values are typical.
2. There are two physical registers assigned to each bit of this MR parameter: designated set point 0 and set point 1. Only the registers for the set point determined by the state of the FSP-WR bit (MR13 OP[6]) will be written to with an MRW command or read from with an MRR command to this address.
3. There are two physical registers assigned to each bit of this MR parameter: designated set point 0 and set point 1. The device will operate only according to the values stored in the registers for the active set point determined by the state of the FSP-OP bit (MR13 OP[7]). The values in the registers for the inactive set point will be ignored by the device and may be changed without affecting device operation.
4. When OP[3] $=1$ the CK signals will be terminated to the value set by MR11 OP[6:4] regardless of the state of the ODT_CA bond pad. This overrides the ODT_CA bond pad for configurations where CA is shared by two or more devices but CK is not, enabling CK to terminate on all devices.
5. When OP[4] $=1$ the CS signal will be terminated to the value set by MR11 OP[6:4] regardless of the state of the ODT_CA bond pad. This overrides the ODT_CA bond pad for configurations where CA is shared by two or more devices but CS is not, enabling CS to terminate on all devices.
6. For system configurations where the CK, CS, and CA signals are shared between packages, the package design should provide for the ODT_CA ball to be bonded on the system board outside of the memory package. This provides the necessary control of the ODT function for all die with shared command bus signals.
7. When OP[5] = 0, CA[5:0] will terminate when the ODT_CA bond pad is HIGH and MR11 OP[6:4] is valid and disable termination when ODT_CA is LOW or MR11 OP[6:4] is disabled. When OP[5] = 1, termination for CA[5:0] is disabled regardless of the state of the ODT_CA bond pad or MR11 OP[6:4].
8. To ensure proper operation in a multi-rank configuration, when CA, CK or CS ODT is enabled via MR11 OP[6:4] and also via MR22 or ODT_CA pad setting, the rank providing ODT will continue to terminate the command bus in all DRAM states including Active, Self-refresh, Self-refresh Power-down, Active Power-down and Precharge Power-down.# 200b: x32 Automotive LPDDR4X/LPDDR4 SDRAM Burst READ Operation - LPDDR4 ATE Condition 

## Burst READ Operation - LPDDR4 ATE Condition

## ${ }^{1} \mathrm{LZ}(\mathrm{DQS}),{ }^{1} \mathrm{LZ}(\mathrm{DQ}),{ }^{1} \mathrm{HZ}(\mathrm{DQS}),{ }^{1} \mathrm{HZ}(\mathrm{DQ})$ Calculation

${ }^{1} \mathrm{HZ}$ and ${ }^{1} \mathrm{LZ}$ transitions occur in the same time window as valid data transitions. These parameters are referenced to a specific voltage level that specifies when the device output is no longer driving ${ }^{1} \mathrm{HZ}(\mathrm{DQS})$ and ${ }^{1} \mathrm{HZ}(\mathrm{DQ})$, or begins driving ${ }^{1} \mathrm{LZ}(\mathrm{DQS})$ and ${ }^{1} \mathrm{LZ}(\mathrm{DQ})$. This section shows a method to calculate the point when the device is no longer driving ${ }^{1} \mathrm{HZ}(\mathrm{DQS})$ and ${ }^{1} \mathrm{HZ}(\mathrm{DQ})$, or begins driving ${ }^{1} \mathrm{LZ}(\mathrm{DQS})$ and ${ }^{1} \mathrm{LZ}(\mathrm{DQ})$, by measuring the signal at two different voltages. The actual voltage measurement points are not critical as long as the calculation is consistent. The parameters ${ }^{1} \mathrm{LZ}(\mathrm{DQS}),{ }^{1} \mathrm{LZ}(\mathrm{DQ})$, ${ }^{1} \mathrm{HZ}(\mathrm{DQS})$, and ${ }^{1} \mathrm{HZ}(\mathrm{DQ})$ are defined as single ended.

## ${ }^{1} \mathbf{L Z ( D Q S )}$ and ${ }^{1} \mathbf{H Z ( D Q S )}$ Calculation for ATE (Automatic Test Equipment)

Figure 163: ${ }^{1}$ LZ(DQS) Method for Calculating Transitions and Endpoint
![img-168.jpeg](img-168.jpeg)

Notes: 1. Conditions for calibration: Pull down driver $R_{O N}=40$ ohms, $V_{O H}=V_{D D Q} / 3$.
2. Termination condition for DQS_t and DQS_C $=50$ ohms to $\mathrm{V}_{\text {SSQ }}$.
3. The $V_{O H}$ level depends on MR22 OP[2:0] and MR3 OP[0] settings as well as device tolerances. Use the actual $V_{O H}$ value for ${ }^{1} \mathrm{HZ}$ and ${ }^{1} \mathrm{LZ}$ measurements.Figure 164: ${ }^{1} \mathrm{HZ}(\mathrm{DQS})$ Method for Calculating Transitions and Endpoint
![img-169.jpeg](img-169.jpeg)

Notes: 1. Conditions for calibration: Pull down driver $R_{O N}=40$ ohms, $V_{O H}=V_{D D Q} / 3$.
2. Termination condition for $\mathrm{DQS}_{-} \mathrm{t}$ and $\mathrm{DQS}_{-} \mathrm{C}=50$ ohms to $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{SSQ}}$.
3. The $V_{O H}$ level depends on MR22 OP[2:0] and MR3 OP[0] settings as well as device tolerances. Use the actual $V_{O H}$ value for ${ }^{1} \mathrm{HZ}$ and ${ }^{1} \mathrm{LZ}$ measurements.

Table 221: Reference Voltage for ${ }^{1} \mathrm{LZ}(\mathrm{DQS}),{ }^{1} \mathrm{HZ}(\mathrm{DQS})$ Timing Measurements

| Measured Parameter | Measured Parameter <br> Symbol | Vsw1 | Vsw2 | Unit |
| :-- | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
| DQS_c Low-Z time <br> from CK_t, CK_c | ${ }^{1} \mathrm{LZ}(\mathrm{DQS})$ | $0.4 \times V_{O H}$ | $0.6 \times V_{O H}$ | V |
| DQS_c High-Z time <br> from CK_t, CK_c | ${ }^{1} \mathrm{HZ}(\mathrm{DQS})$ | $0.4 \times V_{O H}$ | $0.6 \times V_{O H}$ |  |# Micron

Notes: 1. Conditions for calibration: Pull down driver $R_{O N}=40$ ohms, $V_{O H}=V_{D D Q} / 3$.
2. Termination condition for $D Q$ and $D M I=50$ ohms to $V_{S S Q}$.
3. The $V_{O H}$ level depends on MR22 OP[2:0] and MR3 OP[0] settings as well as device tolerances. Use the actual $V_{O H}$ value for ${ }^{1} \mathrm{HZ}$ and ${ }^{1} \mathrm{LZ}$ measurements.

3. The $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}$ level depends on MR22 OP[2:0] and MR3 OP[0] settings as well as device tolerances. Use the actual $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}$ value for ${ }^{1} \mathrm{HZ}$ and ${ }^{1} \mathrm{LZ}$ measurements.

| DQ High-Z time <br> from CK_t, CK_c | ${ }^{1} \mathrm{HZ}(\mathrm{DQ})$ | $0.4 \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}$ | $0.6 \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}$ |  |# $V_{\text {REF }}$ Specifications - LPDDR4 

## Internal $V_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ Specifications

The device's internal $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{REF}(\mathrm{CA})}$ specification parameters are operating voltage range, step size, $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{REF}}$ step time, $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{REF}}$ full-range step time, and $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{REF}}$ valid level.

The voltage operating range specifies the minimum required $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{REF}}$ setting range for LPDDR4 devices. The minimum range is defined by $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{REF}, \max }$ and $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{REF}, \min }$.

## Table 223: Internal $V_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ Specifications

| Symbol | Parameter | Min | Typ | Max | Unit | Notes |
| :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
| $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA),max_r0 }}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ range-0 MAX operating point | $-$ | $-$ | $30 \%$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}$ | 1,11 |
| $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA),min_r0 }}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ range-0 MIN operating point | $10 \%$ | $-$ | $-$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}$ | 1, 11 |
| $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA),max_r1 }}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ range-1 MAX operating point | $-$ | $-$ | $42 \%$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}$ | 1, 11 |
| $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA),min_r1 }}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ range-1 MIN operating point | $22 \%$ | $-$ | $-$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}$ | 1, 11 |
| $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA),step }}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ step size | $0.30 \%$ | $0.40 \%$ | $0.50 \%$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}$ | 2 |
| $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA),set_tol }}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ set tolerance | $-1.00 \%$ | $0.00 \%$ | $1.00 \%$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}$ | $3,4,6$ |
|  |  | $-0.10 \%$ | $0.00 \%$ | $0.10 \%$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}$ | $3,5,7$ |
| ${ }^{1} \mathrm{~V}_{\text {REF }}$ TIME-SHORT | $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ step time | - | - | 100 | ns | 8 |
| ${ }^{1} V_{\text {REF }}$ TIME-MIDDLE |  | - | - | 200 | ns | 12 |
| ${ }^{1} V_{\text {REF }}$ TIME-LONG |  | - | - | 250 | ns | 9 |
| ${ }^{1} V_{\text {REF_time_weak }}$ |  | - | - | 1 | ms | 13, 14 |
| $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA)_val_tol }}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ valid tolerance | $-0.10 \%$ | $0.00 \%$ | $0.10 \%$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}$ | 10 |

Notes: 1. $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ DC voltage referenced to $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2(\mathrm{DC})}$.
2. $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ step size increment/decrement range. $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ at DC level.
3. $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA),new }}=\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA),old }}+\mathrm{n} \times \mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA),step }} ; \mathrm{n}=$ number of steps; if increment, use "+"; if decrement, use "-".
4. The minimum value of $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ setting tolerance $=\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA), new }}-1.0 \% \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}$. The maximum value of $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ setting tolerance $=\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA),new }}+1.0 \% \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}$. For $\mathrm{n}>4$.
5. The minimum value of $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ setting tolerance $=\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA), new }}-0.10 \% \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}$. The maximum value of $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ setting tolerance $=\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA),new }}+0.10 \% \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}$. For $\mathrm{n}<4$.
6. Measured by recording the minimum and maximum values of the $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ output over the range, drawing a straight line between those points and comparing all other $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ output settings to that line.
7. Measured by recording the minimum and maximum values of the $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ output across four consecutive steps ( n $=4$ ), drawing a straight line between those points and comparing all other $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ output settings to that line.
8. Time from MRW command to increment or decrement one step size for $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$.
9. Time from MRW command to increment or decrement $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF,min }}$ to $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF,max }}$ or $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF,max }}$ to $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF,min }}$ change across the $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ range in $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF }}$ voltage.
10. Only applicable for DRAM component level test/characterization purposes. Not applicable for normal mode of operation. $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF }}$ valid is to qualify the step times which will be characterized at the component level.11. DRAM range- 0 or range- 1 set by MR12 OP[6].
12. Time from MRW command to increment or decrement more than one step size up to a full range of $V_{\text {REF }}$ voltage within the same $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{REF}(\mathrm{CA}}$ ) range.
13. Applies when VRCG high current mode is not enabled, specified by MR13 [OP3] $=0 \mathrm{~b}$.
14. ${ }^{t} V_{\text {REF }}$ time weak covers all $V_{\text {REF(CA) }}$ range and value change conditions are applied to ${ }^{t} V_{\text {REF }}$ -TIME-SHORT/MIDDLE/LONG.

# Internal $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ Specifications 

The device's internal $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{REF}(\mathrm{DQ})}$ specification parameters are operating voltage range, step size, $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{REF}}$ step tolerance, $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF }}$ step time and $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF }}$ valid level.

The voltage operating range specifies the minimum required $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{REF}}$ setting range for LPDDR4 devices. The minimum range is defined by $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{REF}, \max }$ and $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{REF}, \min }$.

Table 224: Internal $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ Specifications

| Symbol | Parameter | Min | Typ | Max | Unit | Notes |
| :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
| $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ), max_r0 }}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF }}$ MAX operating point Range-0 | $-$ | $-$ | $30 \%$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$ | 1,11 |

| $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ),max_r1 }}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF }}$ MAX operating point Range-1 | $-$ | $-$ | $42 \%$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$ | 1, 11 |
| $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ),min_r1 }}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF }}$ MIN operating point Range-1 | $22 \%$ | $-$ | $-$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$ | 1, 11 |
| $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ),step }}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ step size | $0.30 \%$ | $0.40 \%$ | $0.50 \%$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$ | 2 |
| $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ),set_tol }}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ set tolerance | $-1.00 \%$ | $0.00 \%$ | $1.00 \%$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$ | $3,4,6$ |
|  |  | $-0.10 \%$ | $0.00 \%$ | $0.10 \%$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$ | $3,5,7$ |
| ${ }^{t} V_{\text {REF }}$ TIME-SHORT | $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ step time | - | - | 100 | ns | 8 |
| ${ }^{t} V_{\text {REF }}$ TIME-MIDDLE |  | - | - | 200 | ns | 12 |
| ${ }^{t} V_{\text {REF }}$ TIME-LONG |  | - | - | 250 | ns | 9 |
| ${ }^{t} V_{\text {REF_time_weak }}$ |  | - | - | 1 | ms | 13, 14 |
| $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ),val_tol }}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ valid tolerance | $-0.10 \%$ | $0.00 \%$ | $0.10 \%$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$ | 10 |

Notes: 1. $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ DC voltage referenced to $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}(\mathrm{DC})}$.
2. $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ step size increment/decrement range. $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ at DC level.
3. $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ), new }}=\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ), old }}+\mathrm{n} \times \mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ),step }} ; \mathrm{n}=$ number of steps; if increment, use "+"; if decrement, use "-".
4. The minimum value of $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ setting tolerance $=\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ), new }}-1.0 \% \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$. The maximum value of $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ setting tolerance $=\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ), new }}+1.0 \% \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$. For $\mathrm{n}>4$.
5. The minimum value of $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ setting tolerance $=\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ), new }}-0.10 \% \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$. The maximum value of $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ setting tolerance $=\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ), new }}+0.10 \% \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$. For $\mathrm{n}<4$.
6. Measured by recording the minimum and maximum values of the $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ output over the range, drawing a straight line between those points and comparing all other $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ output settings to that line.
7. Measured by recording the minimum and maximum values of the $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ output across four consecutive steps ( n $=4$ ), drawing a straight line between those points and comparing all other $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ output settings to that line.
8. Time from MRW command to increment or decrement one step size for $\mathrm{V}_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$.9. Time from MRW command to increment or decrement $V_{\text {REF,min }}$ to $V_{\text {REF,max }}$ or $V_{\text {REF,max }}$ to $V_{\text {REF,min }}$ change across the $V_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ Range in $V_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ Voltage.
10. Only applicable for DRAM component level test/characterization purposes. Not applicable for normal mode of operation. $V_{\text {REF }}$ valid is to qualify the step times which will be characterized at the component level.
11. DRAM range- 0 or range- 1 set by MR14 OP[6].
12. Time from MRW command to increment or decrement more than one step size up to a full range of $V_{\text {REF }}$ voltage within the same $V_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ range.
13. Applies when VRCG high current mode is not enabled, specified by MR13 [OP3] $=0$.
14. ${ }^{\mathrm{t}_{\mathrm{V}} \text { FREF_time_weak }}$ covers all $V_{\text {REF(DQ) }}$ Range and Value change conditions are applied to ${ }^{\mathrm{t}} \mathrm{V}_{\text {REF }}$ TIME-SHOR/MIDDLE/LONG.# 200b: x32 Automotive LPDDR4X/LPDDR4 SDRAM Command Definitions and Timing Diagrams - LPDDR4
