## On-Die Termination for the Command/Address Bus

The on-die termination (ODT) feature allows the device to turn on/off termination resistance for CK_t, CK_c, CS, and CA[5:0] signals without the ODT control pin. The ODT feature is designed to improve signal integrity of the memory channel by allowing the DRAM controller to turn on and off termination resistance for any target DRAM devices via the mode register setting.
A simple functional representation of the DRAM ODT feature is shown below.Figure 167: ODT for CA
![img-172.jpeg](img-172.jpeg)

# ODT Mode Register and ODT State Table 

ODT termination values are set and enabled via MR11. The CA bus (CK_t, CK_c, CS, CA[5:0]) ODT resistance values are set by MR11 OP[6:4]. The default state for the CA is ODT disabled.
ODT is applied on the CA bus to the CK_t, CK_c, CS, and CA signals. The CA ODT of the device is designed to enable one rank to terminate the entire command bus in a multirank system, so only one termination load will be present even if multiple devices are sharing the command signals. For this reason, CA ODT remains on, even when the device is in the power-down or self refresh power-down state.

The die has a bond pad (ODT_CA) for multirank operations. When the ODT_CA pad is LOW, the die will not terminate the CA bus regardless of the state of the mode register CA ODT bits (MR11 OP[6:4]). If, however, the ODT_CA bond pad is HIGH and the mode register CA ODT bits are enabled, the die will terminate the CA bus with the ODT values found in MR11 OP[6:4]. In a multirank system, the terminating rank should be trained first, followed by the non-terminating rank(s).

Table 228: Command Bus ODT State

| CA ODT <br> MR11[6:4] | ODT_CA <br> Bond Pad | ODTD-CA <br> MR22 OP[5] | ODTE-CK <br> MR22 OP[3] | ODTE-CS <br> MR22 OP[4] | ODT State <br> for CA | ODT State <br> for CK | ODT State <br> for CS |
| :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
| Disabled $^{1}$ | Valid $^{2}$ | Valid $^{3}$ | Valid $^{3}$ | Valid $^{3}$ | Off | Off | Off |
| Valid $^{3}$ | 0 | Valid $^{3}$ | 0 | 0 | Off | Off | Off |
| Valid $^{3}$ | 0 | Valid $^{3}$ | 0 | 1 | Off | Off | On |
| Valid $^{3}$ | 0 | Valid $^{3}$ | 1 | 0 | Off | On | Off |
| Valid $^{3}$ | 0 | Valid $^{3}$ | 1 | 1 | Off | On | On |
| Valid $^{3}$ | 1 | 0 | Valid $^{3}$ | Valid $^{3}$ | On | On | On |
| Valid $^{3}$ | 1 | 1 | Valid $^{3}$ | Valid $^{3}$ | Off | On | On |

Notes: 1. Default value.
2. Valid $=\mathrm{H}$ or L (a defined logic level)# Micron 

## 200b: x32 Automotive LPDDR4X/LPDDR4 SDRAM Command Definitions and Timing Diagrams - LPDDR4

3. Valid $=0$ or 1 .
4. The state of ODT_CA is not changed when the device enters power-down mode. This maintains termination for alternate ranks in multirank systems.

## DQ On-Die Termination

On-die termination (ODT) is a feature that allows the device to turn on/off termination resistance for each DQ, DQS, and DMI signal without the ODT control pin. The ODT feature is designed to improve signal integrity of the memory channel by allowing the DRAM controller to turn on and off termination resistance for any target DRAM devices during WRITE or MASK WRITE operation.
The ODT feature is off and cannot be supported in power-down and self refresh modes.# Micron 

## 200b: x32 Automotive LPDDR4X/LPDDR4 SDRAM Command Definitions and Timing Diagrams - LPDDR4

The switch is enabled by the internal ODT control logic, which uses the WRITE-1 or MASK WRITE-1 command and other mode register control information. The value of $\mathrm{R}_{\mathrm{TT}}$ is determined by the MR bits.

Figure 168: Functional Representation of DQ ODT

| Mismatch error, DQ-to-DQ within a channel |  | $0.33 \times V_{D D Q}$ | - | - | 2 | $\%$ | $1,2,3$ |

Notes: 1. The ODT tolerance limits are specified after calibration with stable temperature and voltage. To understand the behavior of the tolerance limits when voltage or temperature changes after calibration, see the following section on voltage and temperature sensitivity.2. Pull-down ODT resistors are recommended to be calibrated at $0.33 \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$. Other calibration points may be required to achieve the linearity specification shown above, for example, calibration at $0.5 \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$ and $-0.1 \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$.
3. DQ-to-DQ mismatch within byte variation for a given component, including DQS (characterized).

$$
\text { DQ-to-DQ mismatch }=\frac{\mathrm{R}_{\mathrm{ODT}}(\mathrm{MAX})-\mathrm{R}_{\mathrm{ODT}}(\mathrm{MIN})}{\mathrm{R}_{\mathrm{ODT}}(\mathrm{AVG})}
$$

4. $R_{Z Q}=240 \Omega \pm 1 \%$ over entire operating range after calibration.

# Output Driver and Termination Register Temperature and Voltage Sensitivity 

When temperature and/or voltage change after calibration, the tolerance limits are widen according to the tables below.

Table 233: Output Driver and Termination Register Sensitivity Definition

| Resistor | Definition <br> Point | Min | Max | Unit | Notes |
| :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
| $R_{\text {ONPD }}$ | $0.33 \times V_{D D Q}$ | $90-\left(d R_{O N d T} \times|\Delta T|\right)-\left(d R_{O N d V} \times|\Delta V|\right)$ | $110+\left(d R_{O N d T} \times|\Delta T|\right)+\left(d R_{O N d V} \times|\Delta V|\right)$ | \% | 1,2 |
| $V_{\text {OHPU }}$ | $0.33 \times V_{D D Q}$ | $90-\left(d V_{O H d T} \times|\Delta T|\right)-\left(d V_{O H d V} \times|\Delta V|\right)$ | $110+\left(d V_{O H d T} \times|\Delta T|\right)+\left(d V_{O H d V} \times|\Delta V|\right)$ |  | 1,2,5 |
| $R_{T T(I / O)}$ | $0.33 \times V_{D D Q}$ | $90-\left(d R_{O N d T} \times|\Delta T|\right)-\left(d R_{O N d V} \times|\Delta V|\right)$ | $110+\left(d R_{O N d T} \times|\Delta T|\right)+\left(d R_{O N d V} \times|\Delta V|\right)$ |  | 1,2,3 |
| $R_{T T(I N)}$ | $0.33 \times V_{D D 2}$ | $90-\left(d R_{O N d T} \times|\Delta T|\right)-\left(d R_{O N d V} \times|\Delta V|\right)$ | $110+\left(d R_{O N d T} \times|\Delta T|\right)+\left(d R_{O N d V} \times|\Delta V|\right)$ |  | 1,2,4 |

Notes: 1. $\Delta \mathrm{T}=\mathrm{T}-\mathrm{T}$ (@calibration), $\Delta \mathrm{V}=\mathrm{V}-\mathrm{V}$ (@calibration)
2. $\mathrm{dR}_{\mathrm{ONdT}}, \mathrm{dR}_{\mathrm{ONdV}}$, $\mathrm{dV}_{\mathrm{OHdT}}, \mathrm{dV}_{\mathrm{OHdV}}$, $\mathrm{dR}_{\mathrm{TTdV}}$, and $\mathrm{dR}_{\mathrm{TTdT}}$ are not subject to production test but are verified by design and characterization.
3. This parameter applies to input/output pin such as DQS, DQ, and DMI.
4. This parameter applies to input pin such as CK, CA, and CS.
5. Refer to Pull-up/Pull-down Driver Characteristics for $\mathrm{V}_{\text {OHPU }}$.

Table 234: Output Driver and Termination Register Temperature and Voltage Sensitivity

| Symbol | Parameter | Min | Max | Unit |
| :-- | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
| $\mathrm{dR}_{\text {ONdT }}$ | $\mathrm{R}_{\mathrm{ON}}$ temperature sensitivity | 0 | 0.75 | $\% / \mathrm{C}$ |
| $\mathrm{dR}_{\text {ONdV }}$ | $\mathrm{R}_{\mathrm{ON}}$ voltage sensitivity | 0 | 0.20 | $\% / \mathrm{mV}$ |
| $\mathrm{dV}_{\text {OHdT }}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}$ temperature sensitivity | 0 | 0.75 | $\% / \mathrm{C}$ |
| $\mathrm{dV}_{\text {OHdV }}$ | $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}$ voltage sensitivity | 0 | 0.35 | $\% / \mathrm{mV}$ |
| $\mathrm{dR}_{\text {TTdT }}$ | $\mathrm{R}_{\mathrm{TT}}$ temperature sensitivity | 0 | 0.75 | $\% / \mathrm{C}$ |
| $\mathrm{dR}_{\text {TTdV }}$ | $\mathrm{R}_{\mathrm{TT}}$ voltage sensitivity | 0 | 0.20 | $\% / \mathrm{mV}$ |

Operation or timing that is not specified is illegal. To ensure proper operation, the device must be initialized properly.

Notes: 1. $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 1}$ uses significantly less power than $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DD} 2}$.
2. The voltage range is for DC voltage only. DC voltage is the voltage supplied at the DRAM and is inclusive of all noise up to 20 MHz at the DRAM package ball.
3. The voltage noise tolerance from DC to 20 MHz exceeding a peak-to-peak tolerance of 45 mV at the DRAM ball is not included in the TdIVW.

## Output Slew Rate and Overshoot/Undershoot specifications - LPDDR4

## Single-Ended Output Slew Rate

Table 236: Single-Ended Output Slew Rate

| Parameter | Symbol | Value |  | Units |
| :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
|  |  | Min | Max |  |
| Single-ended output slew rate $\left(\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}=\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}} / 3\right)$ | SRQse | 3.5 | 9.0 | V/ns |
| Output slew rate matching ratio (rise to fall) | - | 0.8 | 1.2 | - |

Notes: 1. $\mathrm{SR}=$ Slew rate; $\mathrm{Q}=$ Query output; se $=$ Single-ended signal
2. Measured with output reference load.
3. The ratio of pull-up to pull-down slew rate is specified for the same temperature and voltage, over the entire temperature and voltage range. For a given output, it represents the maximum difference between pull-up and pull-down drivers due to process variation.
4. The output slew rate for falling and rising edges is defined and measured between $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OL}(\mathrm{AC})}=0.2 \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}(\mathrm{DC})}$ and $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}(\mathrm{AC})}=0.8 \times \mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}(\mathrm{DC})}$.
5. Slew rates are measured under average SSO conditions with $50 \%$ of the DQ signals per data byte switching.
6. Note 1-5 applies to entire table.

| :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: | :--: |
|  |  | Min | Max |  |

5. Note $1-4$ applies to entire table.

## LVSTL I/O System - LPDDR4

LVSTL I/O cells are comprised of a driver pull-up and pull-down and a terminator.Figure 171: LVSTL I/O Cell
![img-176.jpeg](img-176.jpeg)

To ensure that the target impedance is achieved, calibrate the LVSTL I/O cell as following example:

1. Calibrate the pull-down device against a 240 ohm resistor to $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}}$ via the ZQ pin.

- Set strength control to minimum setting
- Increase drive strength until comparator detects data bit is less than $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{DDQ}} / 3$
- NMOS pull-down device is calibrated to 120 ohms

2. Calibrate the pull-up device against the calibrated pull-down device.

- Set $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}$ target and NMOS controller ODT replica via MRS ( $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}$ can be automatically controlled by ODT MRS)
- Set strength control to minimum setting
- Increase drive strength until comparator detects data bit is greater than $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}$ target
- NMOS pull-up device is calibrated to $\mathrm{V}_{\mathrm{OH}}$ target
